Financial Market Opening Plummets 82

Wild Plunge of 24 Taels

Extremely Strong Fluctuations: The Gold Exchange opened as usual yesterday, February 19th. The gold price rose and fell, but there were still violent changes like a hurricane and a rainstorm. The dangerous situation was irrepressible, and people were terrified. The price fluctuated by as much as 30 taels throughout the day, with a total plummet of more than 20 taels. Opinions among the industry varied, but the confusion was inevitable. Companies like Hengxing, Yuanfu, Chang, and a certain Lu bought and sold repeatedly. Yuanmao, Yongyuan, Taiyuan, and Shengyuan all bought in. Zhifeng, Yongheng, Xinghongli, etc., mostly sold out. The exchange rates on the foreign exchange market shrank by half, while the domestic market improved, creating a stark contrast. As for the overseas silver market, it shrank and then rose, causing the gold price to open low. Later, due to purchases by large investors and tight exchange rates, it rose rapidly and reached the 800-tael mark. Then, a new record of 99 taels was discovered. Later, speculators like a certain Lu suddenly sold off, causing the exchange rate to weaken. Furthermore, with the possibility of the establishment of a Sino-American silver coin loan, general sentiment was stimulated and a storm broke out. The rapid retreat caused a massive drop of more than 20 taels, with a sense of complete collapse. In the after-hours market, Yuanmao, Yong, Zhifengyong, etc., bought in, while Yuanheng, Hongli, and Yuantai sold. The situation remained confusing, with fluctuations of seven to eight taels at times. It once broke the 70-tael mark, and the final count was 72-73 taels. It is said that the large orders this morning may continue to rise.

Once a High Price Was Discovered: The opening price for April in the morning fell by 4 taels and 5 qian to 791 taels. This was because the total number of taels in the past three days was only one-sixteenth lower. The silver price was balanced, and the European market was strong. Private telegrams also increased by one-fourth. Afterwards, there were fluctuations of more than 4 taels, from 92 and a half taels to 88 taels. Then, sellers became active, and Fuchang, Hengyu, and others bought in, jumping by 8 taels and adding up to 96 taels. Exchange rates also rose, with British banks eating one penny eight one two five each for March and May-June. Then Hengxing sold, slightly reducing it by more than 2 taels. First, an announcement was made that a small one two five had been posted. The US dollar on the 25th, with gold adding one and a half points, was 95 taels and 5 qian at that time. Suddenly, it fell back to 3 and a half taels. In an instant, buyers surpassed Heng, and Dadetai, Hengxing, and Yuan competed to buy. Moreover, British gold banks traded 1175 with each other, and Datong ate 27.9375 US dollars in March, suddenly rising by more than 5 taels. At 9:30, it was a new high of 99 taels. In the blink of an eye, the air on the market was bad. It was rumored that the Sino-American loan could be established, so the price of gold should be viewed as small. In short, the minds of general speculators were different, caused by the rush selling of Hengxing, Changsheng Yong, Hengyu, Zhifengyong, etc., and Hengxingyuan suddenly sold out as well, so the price suddenly turned downwards, plummeting by more than 10 taels to 80 taels at 10:30. Then more than 3 taels were added, and then Yongfeng, Fuyu, Chenfeng, Yongshunli, and Wanxing tended to throw everything away and the storm broke out. After that, it had fallen miserably outside of 10 taels. British gold banks were trading at two pennies and one eight seven five in June, and the US dollar at 28.6875 until 11:20, when it suddenly became 70 taels and 5 qian. However, there were highs and lows of three or four taels in between. The market situation was chaotic and unspeakable. Yuanmao, Yongdadetai, Chengshunli, Wanxing, and Hengxingyuan repurchased, so the price pulled up seven or eight taels to 78 and a half taels. The market closed at noon at 75 taels, then decreased to 72 taels and a little. The price has been changed to 863 taels and 4 qian, a drop of 70 taels to 92 or 3 taels. Noon closed at 89 taels.

The Aftermarket Is Extremely Chaotic: The after-hours market opened at 72 and a half taels, then fell from 74 taels and 5 qian to 72 taels. Because the Indian exchange rate rose, and there were still many sellers in the market, only Yuanmao Yong and others still refused to stop, and they immediately raised it to 75 taels. Suddenly, items were sold from hedging, and in April, the British gold bank used two pennies and one eight seven five to trade, suddenly cutting down five or six taels, and suddenly at 2:20 it was 69 and a half taels. Afterwards, Yu Da Yuanmao, Yongzhifengyong came in. At 2:45 it was 77 taels, and the same Taichang Hengyu and others sold out. At 3:00 it was 70 taels and 3 then. Afterwards, the rise and fall were uncertain, with a cycle of more than 4 taels. After 2:30, buyers seemed to be numerous. Mitsui ate British gold one two five each in May, so they rose again by 7 taels. After 4:00 it was 77 taels and 5 qian. In a moment, the sellers became strong. Yuanheng and Hengxing sold out, and the British gold bank bought in needing two pennies and one eight seven five, so it fell again by more than 6 taels. By 4:30 the market closed at 71 taels, a fall of 24 taels and 5 qian compared to before the holiday (16th), and a heavy trade of 2 taels. But there were no large deals on the market. It was found that the maximum price during the day was 99 taels, and the minimum price was 69 and a half taels, a difference of 29 taels and 5 qian. The early market price of goods was 87 taels, the noon price was 72 taels, the late afternoon price was 72 and a half taels, and the market closed at 71 taels. 19th Year of Cloth and Head General Situation 87

Commodity Prices Rising Step by Step, Industry Peers Profiting Greatly

Last year's cloth and head market rose step by step. Whether it was Eastern goods or Western goods, cotton cloth rose sharply. At the end of the year, it jumped a thousand feet. The reason is that the price of gold skyrocketed and the price of silver plummeted. Compared with the spring and winter prices, they are all higher by one-third. The lowest opening price of Eastern goods' Shuangtonglu Zhigong was two qian two fen seven li and a half, Huxinting Biji was two qian two fen and a half, the first Gong Zhigong satin was two qian five fen, and the old flower Zhigong ne was two qian eight fen. The Western goods' Fangli Zhigong ne was two qian two fen, and the striped banling was one qian eight fen. Before the end, Shuangtong business had reached three qian six fen and a half, Huxinting three qian five fen, and the first Gong three qian seven fen. Fangli Zhigong ne was sold out at one qian one fen, and later had to open three qian five fen. The striped banling was three qian to two qian seven fen. During the year, the lowest price of Rengou plain crepe was two taels eight qian and a half, and the highest price was four taels two qian and a half. The lowest price of colored cloth was six qian and a half, and the highest price was nine taels two qian and a half. The difference was huge and unprecedented. Wool silk cloth, red ocean mark, white ocean yarn, and yuan ocean were all priced at record highs. Among the cotton cloths, fine cloth and fine slanting fabrics both reached one tael or more. Coarse cloth and coarse slanting fabrics were six to seven qian. The surplus among industry peers was also the crown of the year. For example, the newly created Xiehe Shentongfeng and others had surpluses of 50,000 to 60,000, and Hongshengyuan Xiexiang Zhaotai and others made even greater profits. The rest were 10,000 to 20,000. The ones that closed down were Meihua, Sheng Fuyuanxiang, and there were very few losses. Only the daily additions were average. In the area of Xiaodongmen, no one failed to profit.

Local News

Protests Against Opium Public Sale from All Circles 91

Yesterday's Joint Meeting

The Anti-Opium Association of the Republic of China and various national anti-opium organizations regard the rumored public sale of opium as extremely important, concerning the future of China's opium prohibition and international credibility. They specifically held a joint meeting of all sectors at the Municipal Chamber of Commerce at 3:30 PM yesterday to discuss countermeasures. Over two hundred representatives from various organizations and individuals attended. Wang Jingqi, Zhou Hanmei, Huang Jiahui, and Li Denghui served as the presidium. The details of the general meeting are as follows: (A) Dr. Tang Shaochuan's proposal: Huang Jiahui reported that Dr. Tang Shaochuan was unable to attend the meeting as scheduled due to a hernia that has been troubling him, preventing him from sitting or standing, and expressed his apologies. He presented his opinions on Dr. Tang Shaochuan's behalf as follows: During the opium prohibition in the late Qing dynasty, I initially advocated strict measures, leading to the signing of the Sino-British Opium Prohibition Treaty, aiming to completely eradicate opium within ten years. Today, the opium scourge is rampant, and prohibition orders are ineffective. All our people should rise up together to petition the government, requesting strict opium prohibition. I believe the government should implement more opium addiction treatment hospitals and issue an order requiring opium addicts to confess their addiction to the government. The government should then mandate admission to hospitals for detoxification within a specified period. During the detoxification period, they should be deprived of their civil rights and required to display "addict" signs to distinguish them. Those who are addicted but do not register for detoxification should be punished. The government should provide the cost of detoxification medicine, while food expenses should be self-supplied. This is the fundamental method for opium prohibition. I hope various organizations will petition the government separately. As for the opium public sale, I believe it will not be realized because the current officials will not adopt such a policy. (B) Dr. Wang Jingqi's proposal: The key points of protesting against the opium public sale are as follows: The opium public sale violates the public's opinion and the late Premier's teachings. Although it is still a rumor, we should jointly protest in advance, considering the importance of the matter, so that everyone knows the public opinion and is not misled by those who promote public sale. On the one hand, we hope that the rumor is inaccurate, but at the same time, we should strive to support the central government's current prohibition policy. In recent years, opium prohibition has been lax, which is undeniable. Now that the internal wars are being quelled, it is time to strictly enforce prohibition. Our fundamental method of protesting against the public sale is to urge and assist in the implementation of the prohibition policy, and to do our best to promote the spirit of the late Premier's anti-drug teachings, so as to avoid the opium prohibition being nominal and providing an excuse for those who advocate public sale. We must understand that this movement is not a matter of opposing people, but of supporting the government's implementation of the opium prohibition policy. It is not a factional dispute, but a dispute of principles. We are fighting to eliminate the opium scourge and preserve the race. I sincerely hope that the people of the country will identify the goal, hold firm to the principles, not be intimidated by power, not be tempted by profit, and move forward bravely to protest to the end. We will surely win the final victory. (C) Resolutions of important cases: (1) Telegraph to the national public, unanimously protesting against the opium public sale; (2) Form a committee to protest against the opium public sale; (3) Various organizations petition the Central Party Headquarters and the National Government separately; (4) Various organizations petition the Legislative Yuan separately to enact laws and regulations to permanently prohibit public sale; (5) Request the Municipal Party Headquarters to publicize and prevent public sale based on the late Premier's teachings; (6) Promote a national campaign to promote opium prohibition; (7) Seek famous figures and important party and state officials to publish articles against public sale; (8) Request the Municipal Party Headquarters to convene a citizens' meeting to express the public's opposition to public sale; (9) Petition the Control Yuan to exercise its supervisory power based on the late Premier's teachings; (10) Petition the government to announce that it will never publicly sell opium; (11) Contact anti-opium branches and public organizations in various provinces to support each other and request the government to stop public sale; (12) Request the press to vigorously publicize and publish special anti-drug issues to expand publicity; (13) Petition the National Government to abolish the special taxes in Hunan and Hubei. (D) The original text of the telegram, immediately drafted as follows: To all national organizations and newspapers, opium public sale is a policy of weakening the country and harming the people. The late Premier had already condemned it and his teachings are clear. The public believes that it is an unchangeable principle. The National Government had previously issued a clear order to abolish it and adopted a plan for complete prohibition. The Kuomintang's program and opium prohibition laws all have concrete provisions. In recent years, opium prohibition has been lax, which is undeniable. Now that the political training has begun, efforts should be made. The Fourth Plenary Session has already resolved to strictly enforce opium prohibition. All nationals are eagerly hoping for the early elimination of the opium scourge. Unexpectedly, rumors of adopting opium public sale have been circulating recently. The rumors are vivid and raise unnecessary suspicions, such as sending personnel to Taiwan to investigate public sale methods. These rumors increase public anxiety. Our association and others feel the danger and cannot remain silent. Therefore, on February 19th, we held a joint meeting in Shanghai and resolved to jointly petition the government to stop the public sale policy. In addition, we hereby inform the national public to unanimously express their disapproval attitude, respect the late Premier's teachings, refuse to surrender to opium, and vigorously support the complete prohibition policy. We urge local authorities to strictly enforce opium prohibition, so as to clear the drug scourge and reassure the people. We hereby telegraph this message and wish you good health. The joint meeting of Shanghai organizations protesting against opium public sale bows and seals.

Postal Workers' Demands Yesterday's News 92

Negotiations Come to an End

The Shanghai Postal Workers' Union, due to financial difficulties, demanded that the postal authorities provide postal workers with a universal housing allowance of ten yuan. Qian Chunqi, the Director-General of Posts, went to Beijing with Yu Feipeng, the Vice Minister of Communications, and Dou Juecang, the Director of the General Affairs Department of the Ministry of Communications, to Shanghai to convene representatives of the Postal Joint Workers' Union and the Postal Workers' Union for negotiations. It has been reported in the previous newspaper. It is now learned that after several negotiations between the two parties in the past two days, the issue has come to an end yesterday. The results agreed upon by both parties have been submitted to Wang Boqun, the Minister of Communications, for approval and implementation.

This newspaper received a telegram from Beijing yesterday stating that Wang Boqun spoke about Shanghai postal workers' demands for housing allowance and universal promotion. Considering only Shanghai, there are 2,800 postal workers, requiring tens of thousands of yuan per month, and 300,000 yuan per year. As for the promotion, the amount is even greater when calculated nationwide. In 1929, the total postal deficit will be nearly 1.1 million yuan. Savings deposits are very profitable, and remittances have a surplus, but they are not universal in remote areas. If this request is accepted, the postal service will be greatly affected, and even bankruptcy is possible. Moreover, the Ministry's budget has been approved by the Central Government, and it is impossible to arbitrarily increase it, which would affect the established financial policy. Furthermore, postal workers' salaries are already more generous than those of workers in other state-owned enterprises and private industrial and commercial enterprises. If they are allowed to demand more, it will cause social injustice. According to reports from various parties, the postal workers' actions are inevitably instigated by others for other purposes. Therefore, the Ministry has specifically sent Vice Minister Yu and others to Shanghai to investigate the truth and handle it accordingly, in order to prevent unfortunate incidents.

Silver and Banking Industry Resumes Normal Business Yesterday 93

The local silver and banking industries took a break on the 17th and 18th, which were the settlement period for the business community. Therefore, financial transactions were completely suspended on the past two days. Business resumed as usual yesterday, but the volume of transactions was one or two times less than usual.

Meningitis Epidemic on the Shanghai-Hangzhou Railway Greatly Reduced 94

Result of Deng Zhende's Active Prevention

Meningitis, an acute infectious disease, was previously discovered in Haining and other places near the Shanghai-Hangzhou Railway. For a time, the epidemic was rampant and there was a danger of it spreading to Shanghai. Deng Zhende, the General Director of the Beijing-Shanghai and Shanghai-Hangzhou Railways, believed that railway vehicles and the large number of passengers were most susceptible to infection. He previously went to Hangzhou with Liu Ruiheng, the Director of the Department of Health of the Ministry of Interior, to discuss several epidemic prevention measures with the Zhejiang Provincial Department of Civil Affairs. Strict precautions were taken at all stations along the Shanghai-Hangzhou Railway, and passengers were inspected and treated at epidemic stations. Since the prevention and treatment, the epidemic has been greatly reduced, and there is no fear of further spread. However, he is still ordering intensified work to eradicate it as soon as possible.

Japanese Consulate Notifies That the Fushun Mine Accident Did Not Injure Chinese Workers 99

The Guowen News Agency reported that the Fushun Coal Mine, run by the Japanese, had an accident on the 8th of this month, and 3,000 Chinese workers died. After the accident, the Japanese Consulate General in Shanghai immediately telegraphed the consuls stationed in Liaoyang and Pingan to inquire about everything in detail. According to the reply telegram, the accident did occur, but there were no casualties. After receiving the telegram, the Consulate General specifically sent a letter to Mayor Zhang Yuejun of this city yesterday to inform all parties and ask them not to misunderstand.

Difficult Birth of the Chinese Director-General of the Public Works Department 100

The Board of Directors Still Did Not Pass the Name Issue Yesterday

The issue of the Shanghai Municipal Council of the Public Works Department hiring Chinese people as commercial-level administrative staff has been delayed for two months. Yesterday afternoon, the Municipal Council held a board meeting, attended by all Chinese and foreign directors. From 4:30 PM to 6:30 PM, the meeting adjourned. The special committee had submitted the issue of the Chinese Director-General for discussion, but the name issue has not been resolved for a long time. The Chinese Director-General of the Public Works Department has become a difficult birth. On the issue, the Chinese directors argued that under the Director-General, there should be two secretaries, one of whom should be a British person, and the other should be a newly hired Chinese person. The British directors believed that the motivation for the Public Works Department to hire a Chinese person as a senior administrative staff member was originally for the convenience of contacting Chinese officials and dealing with Chinese people. Therefore, the initial name was determined to be Chinese Liaison Officer. Later, because the Chinese directors were not satisfied, they agreed to be named Deputy Secretary or Chinese Secretary. In this way, the authority of the Chinese Director-General would be entirely for handling Chinese affairs, and could not interfere with the general responsibilities of the Director-General. The Chinese directors were still not satisfied and insisted that they should be collectively called Director-General, and the word "Chinese" should not be added. The status of the two Director-Generals must be equal externally, and the division of authority is allowed internally. The British directors believed that the name issue was closely related to the future of the concession and was inconsistent with the Land Regulations of the Yangjingbang. Therefore, they still could not compromise. Yesterday's meeting did not yield any concrete results on the name issue. The issue was still referred to the special committee for reconsideration and submitted to the next board meeting for discussion. The issue of candidates was not mentioned. The special committee is scheduled to meet next Monday.

Municipal Health Bureau Revises Regulations for Managing Traditional Chinese Medicine Practitioners 112

Has Been Approved and Promulgated

The Municipal Health Bureau, in order to consider the situation, had previously revised the "Provisional Regulations for Managing Medical Practitioners (Traditional Chinese Medicine) in this City" and submitted them to the Municipal Government for approval. It is now reported that the revised regulations have been approved and promulgated.

Shanghai Municipal Health Bureau Provisional Regulations for Managing Medical Practitioners (Traditional Chinese Medicine) Article 1: All traditional Chinese medicine practitioners operating in this city, before the Central Government promulgates the Medical Practitioner Law, shall comply with these regulations. Article 2: Those traditional Chinese medicine practitioners who have not passed the examination or review according to the regulations will not be registered. Those who have not been registered shall not open a practice in this city. Article 3: The examination or review of traditional Chinese medicine practitioners shall be handled by the Bureau inviting several people of excellent character and learning and rich experience from the traditional Chinese medicine community to form a Traditional Chinese Medicine Examination Committee. Article 4: The traditional Chinese medicine examination shall be held once a year in June. Article 5: Those traditional Chinese medicine practitioners whose qualifications cannot be listed as exempt from the registration examination shall apply for the examination and pay an examination fee of eight yuan. Those who failed the first time and apply for the examination again in the next session shall have their examination fee reduced by half. Article 6: Those who have one of the following qualifications and pass the review shall be allowed to register for exemption from the examination, be issued a license to open a practice, and be exempted from the examination fee: (A) Those who have graduated from a traditional Chinese medicine school approved by the University Council of the National Government and have a diploma; (B) Those who had obtained a business license issued by the Beijing Ministry of Interior or the Health Bureau of Songhu Commercial Port, Guangzhou, Shantou, etc. before this city was established. Article 7: Those traditional Chinese medicine practitioners who have passed the examination or review shall pay a registration and license fee of three yuan per person and a stamp duty of one yuan, all of which shall be paid before obtaining a business license. Article 8: Those traditional Chinese medicine practitioners who are taking the examination shall submit the application form, resume, and two 4-inch half-length photos of themselves according to the prescribed format fifteen days before the scheduled examination, together with the examination fee, to the Bureau for an examination certificate. Article 9: Those who have qualifications for exemption from the examination shall submit the application form, resume, and two 寸半(cun ban, about 1.5 inch) photos of themselves according to the prescribed format fifteen days before the scheduled examination, together with the diploma, certificate, license, and other documents proving their qualifications to the Bureau for review. Article 10: The traditional Chinese medicine examination is divided into written and oral examinations. Those who pass the written examination shall take the oral examination. Those who pass the oral examination shall be allowed to register and be issued a license to open a practice. Article 11: The subjects of the examination are as follows: 1. Outline of Internal Medicine; 2. Outline of Typhoid Fever; 3. Outline of 温病(Wen Bing, Warm Disease); 4. Outline of Epidemic Diseases; 5. Outline of Gynecology; 6. Outline of Surgery; 7. Outline of Pediatrics; 8. Outline of Ophthalmology; 9. Outline of Otorhinolaryngology; 10. Outline of Trauma; 11. Outline of Materia Medica; 12. Outline of Ancient Prescriptions. Among the above twelve subjects, surgery, pediatrics, ophthalmology, otorhinolaryngology, and trauma are now called specialized subjects, but each subject is based on Internal Medicine, and all use Materia Medica, and each has its own scriptures and prescriptions. Therefore, Internal Medicine, Materia Medica, and Ancient Prescriptions are compulsory subjects. As for those who call themselves "大方脈(Da Fang Mai, general medicine)" (1) to (5) and (11) and (12) seven items shall be examined. Article 12: An average score of 70 or more in each subject shall be considered a passing grade. Those who pass the written examination shall take an oral examination to determine acceptance or rejection. Article 13: During the review, if there is any doubt, the Examination Committee may send a letter to the Bureau, notifying the person being reviewed to provide supplementary evidence or to attend a meeting for questioning. Article 14: Those who have passed the review or examination shall be given a medical practitioner's business license. The license shall be claimed within the prescribed time limit. If it is claimed after more than one year, a fine of ten yuan may be imposed, twenty yuan for more than two years, and cancellation for more than three years. Article 15: Those who practice medicine in this city without registering and obtaining a license from the Bureau shall be fined up to 200 yuan and have their business suspended. Article 16: Each doctor shall prepare a clinic book to record the patient's name, age, gender, address, and the name of the disease, treatment method, prescription, number of examinations, etc. for reference, and must be kept for more than two years. Article 17: Each doctor shall guide the disinfection method when diagnosing infectious patients or examining the corpses of infectious diseases to avoid the spread, and report to the Bureau as soon as possible. In case of childbirth or death, a report shall also be made at any time. The format of the report shall be prepared by the Bureau, and each doctor may receive it in advance for use. Article 18: The business license obtained by each doctor shall be posted in a place that is easy for the public to view, and shall be submitted for annual inspection once a year in accordance with the Bureau's regulations, and a stamp shall be issued. Those who fail to submit it for inspection within the time limit shall be fined up to five yuan. Article 19: If the license is lost, it may be applied for replacement. In addition to complying with the provisions of Article 7, a notice shall be published stating that the loss is invalid. Article 20: In case of relocation, each doctor shall report to the Bureau for reference within two weeks. Those who fail to do so shall be fined up to ten yuan. Article 21: These regulations shall be repealed after the medical practitioner's laws and regulations are promulgated. Article 22: If there are any matters not covered in these regulations, they may be amended at any time. Article 23: These regulations shall come into force from the date of approval by the Municipal Government.

Amicable Settlement of the Chunhua Factory Labor Strike 113

The labor strike at the Chunhua Rubber Factory on Jiandaoqiao Road in the Nanshi district of this city, which had been ongoing for some time, had seen the Social Affairs Bureau dispatch personnel for mediation, and both labor and management had also conducted independent negotiations, but without success. Yesterday, at 1:00 PM, the bureau convened a mediation committee to conduct mediation on this case, discussing and signing a three-point agreement: (1) During the factory shutdown period, wages from January 16th to February 10th of this year will be paid by the factory to each worker at a rate of 45 cents per day, according to the previously agreed-upon labor-management terms. From February 11th until the factory reopens, each worker will receive a daily allowance of 20 cents, with meals provided as usual. (2) During the dispute period, workers who did not receive meals will be subsidized 3 yuan each by the factory, except for those who signed up for meals at the factory. (3) The factory will compensate workers for losses suffered in the fire, at 1 yuan per person. This matter was agreed upon and signed by representatives of both parties, and the mediation was successfully concluded. It is subject to tax, similar to a labor contract between the parties involved.

Jisheng Association to Establish Straw Hat Training Center in Beiping 114

The Chinese Jisheng Association recently received letters from Mr. Yu Guisheng, director of the Tianjin office, and Mr. Zhou Jingfu, director of the Beiping office, stating that since the provincial capital of Beiping was moved to Tianjin, more people have become unemployed, and the livelihood of the poor is getting worse year by year. Those who were considered poor in previous years are now extremely poor. Although the association has exclusively established soup kitchens, or invited various charitable organizations to set up soup kitchens, with as many as 25 locations last year, charitable donations are limited, while the number of poor people is increasing endlessly. Continuing to sit idle will lead to inevitable collapse, and it is difficult to provide adequate relief. Moreover, simply feeding the idle is not a good strategy. It is necessary to provide manual labor opportunities and opportunities for production, so that young and middle-aged women have trades they can learn as a basis for making a living, so that the number of poor people will gradually decrease. They requested the establishment of straw hat weaving training centers in two locations in Beiping: Liangjiayuan in the southern city and Huangchenggen in the western city, to collaborate with charitable individuals, raise funds in the name of the association, and recruit women to learn the craft. Currently, 300 female students have registered, with each student requiring about 4 yuan per month for meals. Based on individual aptitude, the training period will be two months or four months. After completing their studies, they will be assessed and paid wages to support their livelihoods. Now, Mr. Lin Ziwen has been sent to Shanghai to discuss funding matters. The association has initially agreed to set up two locations, with the association responsible for the start-up expenses and the daily meals for the female students. If successful in the future, it will be further promoted. This is also a fundamental method of relieving the poor. It is hoped that charitable comrades at home and abroad will emulate this approach, so that poor women can earn their own living.

The Tragic Situation of the Shaanxi Disaster 115

The Sino-Foreign Relief Association Earnestly Hopes for Assistance

The Shanghai Sino-Foreign Relief Association received a telegram yesterday from the Shaanxi Association stating, "The Shaanxi disaster is severe, compounded by heavy snowfall, with people freezing and starving, corpses everywhere, and no one to bury them. The situation is heart-wrenching. The elderly and weak from all over are flocking to the provincial capital, but there is no way to save them. Watching them freeze to death fills us with shame and unspeakable remorse. We earnestly request your assistance, great compassion, and universal salvation of the survivors. The telegram is extremely urgent, awaiting orders. The Shaanxi Sino-Foreign Relief Association, in the cold." It is reported that the Shanghai association has already remitted funds in succession and is still making every effort. However, the disaster is too severe, and it is difficult to raise relief funds. It is earnestly hoped that all sectors will provide assistance.

Public Buses to Operate in Gaoqiao, Pudong 119

From the Town to the Ferry Terminal

Gaoqiao Town in Pudong has a large population and abundant local resources. Many residents operate various businesses in Puxi, so their need for reliable and fast transportation is extremely urgent. Since the municipal government's ferry service started operating new ferries, people in the town have repeatedly requested the authorities to extend the service to Gaoqiao. In order to meet the needs, the Municipal Public Works Bureau has added two ferries, which have already been completed. As soon as the Gaoqiao pier is completed, the service can be opened. However, due to the large ships and small harbor, they cannot sail close to the pier site in the town, which is about 1.3 kilometers from the town. The bureau believes that without adequate land transportation links, travel will still be inconvenient. Therefore, it is planned to operate public buses from Gaoqiao Town to the ferry terminal, connecting with the ferry schedule. Roads and bridges have also been built. It is reported that this plan has been approved by the municipal government and is currently being actively prepared by the bureau, using the latest type of buses, to be implemented simultaneously with the ferry service.

Routes 3 Temporarily Suspended... Route 2 in South Shanghai Detoured

The Huashang Route 3 public bus in the Chinese area of this city, from the North Railway Station to the Zhenru area, has been experiencing difficulties due to the muddy roads caused by continuous rain and snow. In order to maintain the safety of passengers, the company reported to the Municipal Public Works Bureau and was approved to temporarily suspend operations from 4:00 PM on the 14th of this month, and resume normal operations after dark. Also, Route 2 of the South Shanghai Public Bus, from Laoximen to Longhua Town, Rongzhong Kang Road and Longhua Road, has also been affected by rain and snow, with loose soil making it inconvenient to drive. It is reported that agreement has been reached with the Public Works and Engineering Bureaus to detour via Zhizaoju Road, enter Xietu Road directly to Zhaoji Road, and then enter Longhua Town. Operations will resume on the original route after the weather clears and the roads are repaired.

Commodity Inspection Bureau Relieves Local Bovine Plague 123

Free Serum Injections for Milk Farms

The Shanghai Commodity Inspection Bureau has been studying methods for preventing livestock diseases since March of last year, under the direction of the Livestock Products Inspection Office. It also began manufacturing bovine plague serum, renting several acres of private land in Jiangwan for testing. At the beginning, due to limited funding, all facilities were still simple. However, its products have been tested repeatedly, and the results are still satisfactory. Last autumn, at the request of the Jiangsu Provincial Department of Agriculture and Mining, the bureau sent personnel to various villages in Qianbeixiang in the fourth district of Zhenjiang to inject serum, curing more than 50 cattle in total. In the spring, the Shanghai Livestock Planting Company purchased four valuable purebred calves from the Red Flower Milk Company in Seattle, USA, and also requested the bureau to inject serum to ensure their health. Recently, bovine plague broke out in Shanghai and is rampant. Through the introduction of Ma Wenjia and Jiang Weiliang of the Dairy Industry Association, Cai Ji, deputy director and veterinarian of the bureau, accompanied by veterinarian Shou Biao and others, went to various milk farms to inject serum free of charge. These included the Huasheng Milk Farm on Huasheng Road, the Huili Milk Farm on Zhoujiazui Road, and the Hongkou Milk Farm and Huishan Milk Farm in Hongkou, saving more than 20 cattle in total. Among them, three were in particularly critical condition and were refused treatment by a well-known Shanghai veterinarian. They were also cured by the bureau using serum. All the cattle owners praised the effectiveness of the serum. In light of past achievements, and because this undertaking is emphasized and promoted by Minister Kong, the bureau is now preparing to submit a request to the Ministry of Industry for permission to actively expand equipment and manufacture more serum to meet the needs of various regions and alleviate the difficulties of farmers.

Robbery and Assault Case This Morning 127

Chu Chaoding Seriously Injured

At about half past midnight this morning, Chu Chaoding, a 33-year-old from Henan, and Chen Zhengji, a rickshaw puller from Jiangbei, were passing through Songshan Road in the French Concession when they heard someone calling for help. They immediately followed the sound and saw several bandits blocking passersby and carrying out their killing work. When the bandits saw people coming, they immediately opened fire on them. Unexpectedly, Chu's right waist and Chen's right lower abdomen were each hit by a bullet, and the bullets did not pass through. Patrolman No. 307 of the French Police Station heard the sound and went to the scene, but the bandits had already escaped without a trace. The injured two were then taken by car to the police station to report, and then taken to Renji Hospital for treatment. It is reported that Chu Chaoding's injuries are extremely serious, and there is fear for his life.

Hezong Box Factory in Litigation with Jin Xing Insurance Company 128

Jin Xing Unwilling to Pay a Thousand Taels, Court Orders Re-survey

The Hezong Machine Box Factory had insured against fire with Jin Xing Insurance Company for 2,000 taels of silver. In August of the year before last, a fire broke out, and the front buildings of the factory were completely burned down. Fortunately, the fire brigade made every effort to rescue the situation, so the machine installation part in the rear was able to survive. Afterwards, Jin Xing Company specially invited experts to estimate the fire loss. Because the factory was located in the Zhabei Chinese area, they refused foreigners to go to the factory for inspection, so Jin Xing refused to compensate. The company was sued in court. After trial, the court ruled that since only half of the burned buildings were burned, the defendant should compensate for 1,000 taels of insurance. Jin Xing refused to accept this decision and hired a lawyer to appeal to the Higher Branch Court. The reason given was that the burned house was of a very simple structure and not connected to the unburned part of the factory, so it was not covered by the insurance. Even if it was connected to the unburned part, the construction cost would certainly not be equal to the unburned part. In order to compensate for the loss, it is necessary to estimate the value of the burned house in order to show fairness. However, the original judgment ordered compensation based on the reason that half was burned, which is difficult to convince. Yesterday afternoon, Hu Yigu, the presiding judge of the Civil Division of the High Court, judges Li Mo and Gao Junxiang, and clerk Qian Qizhong, held a hearing. First, the lawyer for the appellant stated the reasons, and then the respondent also hired a lawyer to respond. The court believed that the degree of the fire could not be clarified without a personal inspection of the factory, so it ordered both parties to pay 10 yuan each for the survey fee within seven days, and a hearing would be held after the survey was clarified. However, the burned house has already been rebuilt and completed by the factory, and there is no trace of the fire damage left, so the survey may be very difficult.

Merchants and Residents Love Director Tao of the First Precinct of the Fifth District 129

Presentation of a Large Silver Shield

Wu Zhaoji and other merchants and residents in the area of North Sichuan Road and Qiujiang Road in Zhabei presented a large silver shield with the inscription "Protect Merchants and Defend the People" to Tao Xian, director of the First Precinct of the Fifth District of the Municipal Public Security Bureau, in order to express their gratitude for the close and conscientious defense work and protection of merchants and residents.

Local News Two

Zou Aizhen Counter-Sues Tang Huixuan: Trial Begins 131

Accusation of False Accusation and Bigamy

Bigamy Seems to Have Exceeded Statute of Limitations

The False Accusation Needs Investigation

Economic Doctor Tang Huixuan, also known as Tang Chongci, sued his wife Zou Aizhen (also known as Zou Weici) for adultery with Chen Genwei, but the case was not established. Zou Aizhen counter-sued Tang Huixuan for false accusation and bigamy, and a public prosecution was initiated.

Tang Huixuan's two written documents are used as evidence for the bigamy charge. Zou Aizhen submitted two papers written by Tang Shuli: (One) the original text is: "Chongci hereby writes the following document with the utmost sincerity: If I break my promise midway, I will accept any punishment from Aizhen and will never disobey. (1) When Chongci and Aizhen got engaged, I did not explain everything, so Aizhen only knew about Chongci and no one else. In the future, if any person surnamed Tang comes to claim kinship or create trouble, Aizhen can use any means to deal with them, and Chongci shall have no objection. (2) When Chongci and Aizhen got engaged, Chongci had no permanent property. Aizhen often provides economic assistance. In the future, when Chongci becomes successful, Aizhen shall personally manage all movable and immovable property and dispose of it freely. No one from the Tang family or others shall interfere, and Chongci shall obey unconditionally. (3) After Chongci and Aizhen are married, all residential issues and Chongci's actions must be agreed upon by Aizhen, and it is decided that he will never return to Guangxi. If it is necessary to return to Guangxi for important matters concerning Chongci's future, it must also be with Aizhen's permission, and no one from the Tang family shall interfere, and Chongci shall obey unconditionally. (4) After Chongci and Aizhen are married, I am willing to love Aizhen with a pure spirit, and will forever abandon bad habits such as gambling, excessive drinking, taking concubines, and frequenting prostitutes, and will not have relationships with other women. If Chongci breaks this promise, Aizhen is free to punish him." Written by Tang Chongci on October 10th, the twelfth year of the Republic of China. (Two) The original text is: "Tang Chongci, the person writing this separation agreement, because when Tang Chongci and Zou Weici (i.e., Aizhen) got engaged, Chongci did not declare to Weici that he had been married in Guangxi and had children, etc., and only after the marriage did I realize that Chongci admitted to having deceived her. Therefore, a contract was drawn up. After returning to China, Chongci repeatedly violated the contract, and Weici repeatedly tried to dissuade him but he would not listen, proving that he intentionally broke the contract and was deceitful. Therefore, Weici could no longer bear it, and both parties agreed to separate for two years so that Chongci could reform himself. After two years, we would reconcile as before; otherwise, we would divorce formally. During these two years of separation, Chongci must send all income and savings, except for the cost of food, clothing, housing, and transportation, to Weici. All his actions must also be with Weici's permission and must not be violated. In order to avoid empty words without proof, this is written as evidence." Written by Tang Chongci on May 27th in Yichang (Year 18, written on stationery with Hubei stamp tax from the Yichang branch).

Tang Huixuan's testimony record is that Zou Aizhen re-engaged lawyer Zheng Xiuxiu (with lawyer Wang Deyi as a substitute) to submit a statement, requesting a private prosecution for damages. Yesterday morning at 11:00 a.m., Judge Zhao Yongzhou opened the first courtroom to hear the case. Tang Huixuan hired lawyers Qian Shusheng and Yuan Yang'an to defend him in court. Official (asked): Tang Huixuan, also known as Tang Chongci, age 37, from Guangxi, lives by writing, currently an editor at Datong Bookstore, residing at No. 19, Jincheng Lane, Daxing Street. Official (asked): What is your wife's surname at home? (Answer): Her surname is Jiang, she is dead. (Asked): What year did you marry her? (Answer): Married in the third year of the Republic of China, divorced in the seventh year. (Asked): When did you go abroad? (Answer): The eighth year of the Republic of China. (Asked): Why did you divorce and go abroad? (Answer): Because she was disobedient to my parents and did not follow the rules of womanhood. (Asked): Was your divorce by agreement or by judgment? (Answer): It was by agreement. (Asked): Do you have any evidence? (Answer): Yes, it is at home now. (Asked): Did you bring it? (Answer): No. (Asked): Is there any other proof? (Answer): Many relatives and friends at home know about it. (Asked): This is your word against theirs. (Answer): This Jiang died in the eighth year of the Republic of China. (Asked): Do you have proof of her death? (Answer): I know she died. (Asked): This is your word against theirs. (Answer): All my friends know. (Asked): Real evidence is required to count. (Answer): Relatives and friends can all testify for me. (Asked): Are your parents alive? (Answer): Yes. (Asked): How many brothers do you have? (Answer): Three. (Asked): When did you marry Zou Aizhen? (Answer): The twelfth year of the Republic of China. (Asked): Where? (Answer): San Francisco. (Asked): Four days after the marriage, did you receive a letter from home saying your wife was doing well? (Answer): No. However, Zou Aizhen said she was a modern woman from Shanghai and did not want to be a concubine. (Asked): Did she not question you, and did you not write a guarantee yourself? (See the original text above). (Answer): This is a false accusation, it didn't happen. (Asked): Where did the documents she submitted to the court come from? (Answer): They are forged. (Asked): How many children did you have with Aizhen? (Answer): Four, two are still alive, one boy and one girl. (Asked): Why are you in litigation? (Answer): She argued with me and had an affair with Chen Genwei. I was heartbroken, so I sued him. (Asked): When did she have an affair with Chen Genwei? (Answer): From October of the seventeenth year of the Republic of China. I came back from Guangxi and saw their intimate state. Later, the maid told me, so I reported it to the Third Sub-district of the First District and sent two patrol officers to arrest them. This happened on August 16th of last year. (Asked): What is the relationship between Chen Genwei? (Answer): None. (Asked): What about with Zou Aizhen? (Answer): Also none. When I asked, she claimed he was her mother's adopted son, but Chen's own nephew came to testify, proving there was no relationship. (Asked): You once sued for interference with marriage, but the first instance ruled you not guilty. After your appeal was rejected for procedural reasons, it was sent to the prosecutor's office for investigation, and you were not prosecuted? (Answer): Yes. However, Prosecutor Wu said on February 22nd, "This prosecutor is very clear about your case, but you are suffering mentally and financially from being in litigation with them. Why not withdraw the case?" Because I respected the prosecutor's opinion, I stated how they had counter-sued me. The prosecutor said that was not a problem either, so I submitted a statement withdrawing the lawsuit. After receiving the non-prosecution disposition, I wanted to settle the matter peacefully. However, on the eighth day, I received another indictment. This was beyond my expectations. (Asked): After withdrawing the case, did you go to court? (Answer): No. The official said: "This is the false accusation part. You need to provide evidence for the bigamy." (Answer): These documents are forged. But regarding the false accusation, I used to be a professor at Datong University, why would I damage my reputation? (Asked): When did you separate? (Answer): August of the eighteenth year of the Republic of China. She refused to live with me.

Zou Aizhen's testimony generally. The official (asked): Zou Aizhen, (testified): Also known as Zou Weici, age 26, from Shanghai, residing at No. 122, Dananmen, currently unemployed. (Asked): Are you not a teacher? (Answer): My reputation is ruined, I can't be a teacher anymore. (Asked): When did you marry Tang Huixuan? (Answer): October 4th of the twelfth year. (Asked): Where did you get married? (Answer): Inside a church in San Francisco, USA. (Asked): Who introduced you? (Answer): Dong Xiujie. (Asked): Is he Chinese? (Answer): Yes, he is from Nanjing. (Asked): Did he return to China? (Answer): Yes, he has returned to China, and I don't know where he is now. (Asked): Does Tang have a previous wife? (Answer): Yes. (Asked): Did you know when you got married? (Answer): No. Four days after the marriage, a letter came from his family with the words "wife and children are well." I was afraid of being laughed at as a concubine, so he wrote a document to prove that I could gain a foothold in society. (Asked): When was the document written? (Answer): October 10th. (Asked): Now he doesn't admit it. (Answer): You can compare the handwriting. There is also a separation agreement, written on May 27th of the eighteenth year. (Asked): Where is the paper? (Answer): It has already been submitted to the court. (Asked): He said that he came back from Hubei in the eighteenth year and you refused to live with him. (Answer): He forged stamps himself in Yichang and was wanted. He fled to Hankou and took his accountant, Le Zifang, who was sentenced to six months in prison. He was afraid that people would find him, so he dared not live at home and wanted me to live with him in the concession. You can check the judgment. He is slandering me. How can a wife refuse her husband? When I arrived in Yichang, he had already rented a house with a prostitute and was living with her. I wanted to divorce him, so he wrote a separation agreement to see how things would go. (See the original text above). (Asked): If he didn't come to your house, why would he write a separation agreement? (Answer): It was written in Yichang, in May. Le Zifang can testify. Moreover, this stationery is from the office. I could not have forged it. (Asked): What office? (Answer): The Stamp Tax Bureau. (Asked): What did he do? (Answer): He was the director. The official then turned (asked): Regarding Tang's proof that he already had a wife at home, how can this stationery prove it is American? Zou Aizhen (answered): There is a street in America with entirely Chinese shops (Chinatown). (Asked): Did you not have an affair with Chen Genwei? (Answer): No. (Asked): What is the relationship between Chen Genwei and you? (Answer): Siblings. (Asked): He is surnamed Chen and you are surnamed Zou, how can you be siblings? (Answer): He is adopted. (Asked): When was he adopted? (Answer): At the age of six. (Asked): How old is he this year? (Answer): Twenty-eight years old. (Asked): Tang Huixuan said you had an affair with Chen Genwei, so he sued you. (Answer): This is because he wants a divorce unconditionally and is making a false accusation. (Asked): Is there any proof of his adoption? (Answer): Tang Zouqiu. (Asked): Is there anyone else? (Answer): Many relatives know. (Asked): You still need to provide evidence of the adoption. (Answer): My mother is in charge of this. (Asked): What is your mother's name? (Answer): Zou Yu.

The Statute of Limitations for Bigamy Prosecution. At this point, Tang Huixuan added, "I was in Hankou because of illness. She is completely slandering me. Chen Genwei went to England at the age of twenty and had an affair with a friend's wife. He was almost beaten to death and fled back. I paid for Zou Aizhen's tuition and education expenses. I have spent ten years of savings. If she accuses me of bigamy and falsely accuses me, I have no choice but to commit suicide." At this point, the official said that the case still needs to be investigated. Lawyer Qian Shusheng then said, "Assuming Tang Huixuan is suspected of bigamy, it cannot be established now. The bigamy occurred in the twelfth year of the Republic of China. According to Article 11 of the Implementation Law of the Criminal Law, the statute of limitations for the right to prosecute under the old criminal law should be applied, and it has already expired. The prosecutor did not pay attention when prosecuting. To save time, please pay attention to the presiding judge." Then, lawyer Yuan Yang'an added that according to Article 291 of the old criminal law, the most severe punishment for bigamy is imprisonment for a term of four. According to Article 69, Section 5 of the same law, the statute of limitations for public prosecution expires after one year. This case cannot be established at all. The interrogating official then said that the false accusation part still needs to be investigated, so he must be summoned again. The lawyers said yes, and then the court adjourned, waiting for a rescheduled hearing.

A Rogue Son Stabs His Mother with an Awl 132

Gong Yinsheng is Unfilial and Wicked

An old woman from Pudong, Gong Xia, 49 years old, runs a safety pin shop at No. 2, Lane 389, Lujiabang Road, Nanshi. Her husband died early, leaving behind a son and a daughter. The son's name is Yinsheng, 27 years old. The daughter's name is Liubao, 20 years old. Yinsheng is violent and dissolute, and only associates with rogues. The old woman has repeatedly rebuked him but he would not repent. So, last year, she drove him out and did not recognize the mother-son relationship. However, he still went to the old woman's house from time to time to ask for money. The old woman could not bear it. Yesterday afternoon at about 3:00 p.m., Yinsheng and his mistress went directly to the old woman's house and forcibly demanded money. The old woman refused because he had been asking for money repeatedly. Yinsheng became furious and immediately grabbed a very sharp awl from the table and stabbed the old woman wildly. His sister Liubao rushed forward to stop him and was also affected, resulting in numerous wounds and blood flowing like a stream on both the mother and daughter's arms and other places. Wu Yanyi, the security guard of the 26th post in the area, heard about the incident and rushed to the scene, arresting Yinsheng and taking him and the weapon to the First Sub-district of the First District for preliminary interrogation and handling.

Guaranteed Someone Else's Debt and Committed Suicide 133

Qian Mingfu Escaped Without a Trace, Zhang Jinshan Died by Poisoning

Zhang Jinshan, a native of Zhenjiang, 55 years old, was an employee in the color printing department of the Commercial Press on Baoshan Road in Zhabei, with a monthly salary of 50 yuan. He had been working in the library for more than ten years. He had a close friend named Qian Mingfu, who was in the foreign goods business. After closing his business in the middle of last year, he stayed in Shanghai, destitute. He wanted to become a street vendor, but he lacked capital. Through Zhang's introduction, he purchased goods on credit from a foreign goods store on Haining Road, and Zhang guaranteed everything. Initially, the amount was small, but after the Mid-Autumn Festival, the debt gradually increased. By the end of the year, he owed about 600 yuan, but he kept making excuses to return the money, and then disappeared. The store became alarmed and had no choice but to seek payment from the guarantor. They repeatedly demanded payment from Zhang. On the dawn of the lunar New Year's Day, the collectors were still there at 4:00 or 5:00 a.m. Zhang was honest and suffered for others, feeling depressed. The day before yesterday (the 18th), he committed suicide by swallowing opium paste. His colleagues in the dormitory discovered it and immediately sent him to Tongren Hospital for treatment. However, he had been poisoned too much and died at about 5:00 p.m.

Wu Changtai's Sand Boat Encountered Pirates 134

Wu Changtai's sand boat, from Nanshi, recently loaded goods worth thirty to forty thousand taels from Jiaozhou, Shandong, and sailed to Shanghai to be sold on consignment. On the 13th of this month, when sailing in the Yanggang sea area, about twenty miles away from Chongming, a large three-masted ship suddenly sailed in front of them and ordered them to stop. Wu's boat did not suspect it was a pirate ship, so they did not stop and continued sailing as usual. Suddenly, the pirate ship opened fire and injured two of Wu's crew. The crew members were shocked and frightened. A group of pirates swarmed onto the boat, searched everywhere, and only managed to steal more than one hundred yuan. They were furious and immediately forced Wu's boat to sail near Tongzhou, where they robbed half of the cargo on the boat, fully loaded the pirate ship, and fled. Wu's boat is now docked at the mouth of Chongming, but the hull was hit by bullets and cannot sail. The injured crew members were sent to the hospital for treatment.

Died from Blowing Foreign Bubbles 135

The Tragic Death of Ma Xiaosanzi

Ma San, a coolie foreman at the wharf in Nanshi, had a son named Xiaosanzi, 13 years old. Because of the Lunar New Year holiday, Ma was resting at home. Yesterday morning, a relative came to visit Ma for the New Year. Ma invited him to lunch. The relative and Ma's son went out to play and came to a nearby toy stall. Xiaosanzi was happy to see the toys. The relative bought him a foreign bubble-blowing toy and gave it to him to play with. Xiaosanzi took it home and immediately put the bubble tube in his mouth in front of the door, blowing the bubbles bigger or smaller. Unexpectedly, he sucked too hard, and with a sudden contraction, he sucked the bubble into his throat. He was immediately speechless, unable to vomit, and his face turned pale. His parents were shocked and frightened when they saw this. They checked his throat but could not see anything. Later, they hired a car to send Xiaosanzi to Nanshi Hospital for treatment. The doctor examined him and found that the bubble skin had shrunk into the intestinal area below the throat. The bubble was made of water, and the poison mixed into the intestines had already rotted. Although the doctor tried to remove the broken bubbles, the intestinal area was too badly rotted to be saved. He died at 4:00 p.m. His parents hugged his body and cried loudly, heartbroken. Those who saw it were saddened.

Chauffeur Forcibly Defiled a Maid 136

Xiao A'mei, a maidservant at the home of a Dr. Gu at No. 73 Minhang Road, was only 14 years old. She was originally from Suzhou and had been a maidservant in the Gu family for only five months. The day before yesterday at 11:30 a.m., Xiao A'mei went upstairs for something and saw Gu's chauffeur, Jiang Huagen (20 years old) from Wuxi, burning a stove in the wing room. As soon as Xiao A'mei entered the room, she was pushed to the floor by Jiang, who pulled off her clothes and raped her. Xiao A'mei screamed and cried, but there was no one upstairs, and no one downstairs heard anything. After Jiang had satisfied his lust, she was able to get up. Then her uncle, Zhu Heshang, arrived, and Xiao A'mei told him. Zhu told the employer, who informed the Hongkou Police Station, who sent a detective to arrest Jiang. Xiao A'mei was immediately sent to the hospital, where the doctor confirmed that her hymen had been damaged. Yesterday morning, Jiang was taken to the Special District Local Court, where Judge Xiao interrogated him. Zhang Tianyin, the lawyer for the police station, charged Jiang with the crime of raping a minor girl according to Article 140, Section 3 of the Criminal Law and presented the doctor's report and bloodstained pants as evidence. Then, Xiao A'mei recounted the circumstances of the rape. Jiang confessed that he had been a chauffeur in the Gu family for six years. He claimed that what happened yesterday was initiated by Xiao A'mei, who first sat on his lap. He then asked her to go to a hotel with him, but she was too impatient, so this indecent act occurred, and so on. The judge then appointed Shen Xingxia as the defendant's lawyer to defend him. In the end, the defendant was still detained, awaiting a scheduled sentence.

The Ministry of Education Decides to Issue School Fees in Full on a Monthly Basis 141

To Prevent Shortages Again

And Orders All Subordinates to Strive to Improve School Regulations

The Ministry of Education believes that at this time of rectifying the academic atmosphere, it is necessary to find ways to reorganize the education funds in various places. The budget for all schools in the 19th year has been reviewed and submitted to the Central Political Conference for verification. After the reorganization of the school fees this year, it has been decided that they will be issued monthly no matter what, so as to prevent shortages again. It also ordered all subordinates to strive to improve school regulations. The funds for January have been issued one after another by the ministry. It is reported that the ministry has decided to consult with the Ministry of Finance to reissue the funds owed last year.

Jiangsu Education Department's Order to Report the 20th Year's Administrative Plan and Education Budget 143

The Jiangsu Education Department instructed the county magistrates, stating: "The education administrative plan is the basis for annual education facilities, and the education budget should be carefully allocated according to the projects specified in the plan to make the best use of public funds and ensure the successful completion of all tasks. These two are mutually causal and should not be neglected. Since its establishment, this department has deeply understood the relationship between them. Therefore, last year, on one hand, it issued outlines and detailed rules for budget preparation, setting a deadline for submission, and on the other hand, it urged the prompt reporting of administrative plans as a guideline. In the past six months, after repeatedly examining the plans reported by various counties, they often exceeded the budget scope. Even though the budget had been stipulated, projects continued to expand, resulting in numerous requests to draw from the first reserve fund, which seemed to be undisciplined and lacked standards. Both the plan and the budget lost their effectiveness. It was found that the Central Political Council resolved that 'the budget for the 20th year should be prepared before March of the 20th year.' This was previously ordered by the Jiangsu Provincial Government and the Ministry of Education, and it was relayed for compliance. Now that the deadline is approaching, both the budget and the plan should be prepared immediately. This department, in view of the previous discrepancy between the plan and the budget, if not corrected immediately, it will inevitably become unmanageable. Moreover, the economic conditions of various counties have been fluctuating recently, and items such as 'overdue fines' and 'surcharges' have been allocated to the provincial treasury or the collection has been stopped, and the compensatory measures have not yet been resolved. If we do not prepare in advance, the difficulties in the future will only increase. For the sake of prior supervision and assessment, a special order is issued to the county magistrates to supervise their respective bureau chiefs to quickly formulate an education administrative plan for the 20th year based on the actual local economic conditions, and to prepare the education budget for the entire county for the 20th year in strict accordance with the plan. All should be sent to the department for review before March 31st of this year. The content of this plan includes four categories: 'administration,' 'general education,' 'compulsory education,' and 'social education.' The 'general,' 'compulsory,' and 'social' categories must be divided into two parts: 'consolidation' and 'expansion,' to clarify the details and facilitate review. The budget should still be handled in accordance with the outline and detailed rules for preparing education budgets for various counties issued in the 19th year. Fearing that there may still be misunderstandings or unclear points, another copy of the 'Points to Note for Preparing the 20th Year's Budget for Various Counties' is issued, and should be followed. In addition to separate orders, this order is for the county magistrates to comply with. This matter is an important policy for the year, and the county magistrates bear the responsibility for the entire county's education administration, and cannot be negligent, resulting in delays and disciplinary action. Let each be cautious." Attached: "Points to Note" (1) The annual repair and placement expenses required by each school and institution should be extracted by the bureau as a lump sum and listed in the temporary expenditure section to be used for selective disbursement at any time. Unless there is an unexpected and huge use, do not arbitrarily request to use the first reserve fund. (2) The second reserve fund is set up for famine relief and to offset the difference between the assessed amount and the actual collection amount. Counties with a large average difference between the assessed amount and the actual collection amount should list it according to this difference ratio, but counties with a very small difference should not be less than the prescribed amount. (3) Special funds for compulsory and social education to subsidize administrative and special expenses should be listed separately in the compulsory and social education sub-volumes to facilitate the calculation of the amount when checking the issuance and disbursement documents. (4) Under items such as overdue fines and surcharges, the original collection amount and whether there are offsetting measures should be noted for review."

The Kunshan Xu Gongqiao Rural Improvement Society was established by the China Vocational Education Society to test and promote rural vocational education. Since its establishment less than three years ago, it has been proceeding in an orderly manner according to the planned plan, and all facilities have been adopted by those engaged in rural improvement. Yesterday, the society re-elected committee members. Although the snow had just melted and the roads were slippery, more than 200 members still signed in. Guests included Huang Renzhi, Jiang Wenyu, Wu Cuilun, Yao Huiquan, etc. The meeting was held at 1:00 PM, and Cai Wangzhi was publicly elected as chairman to perform the ceremony as usual. Among them, 619 school-age children have enrolled in 468 schools. There are 3 public primary schools and 1 private primary school. The area has 8,922 mu of farmland. Last year, the total income of village fertilizer was 224,506 yuan, and the total expenditure was 196,579 yuan. There were 328 households with surplus. As for the stone roads that have been completed, they reached 3 li, 8 bridges have been repaired, and 5 li of dirt roads have been built. The credit cooperative's business is over 4,000 yuan, and the public clinic treats an average of 3 people per day. Other projects such as farms, fish farming, chicken farming, lace making, and cooperative rice milling have been implemented in sequence. This year, the establishment of small parks and sports fields, Guanlan Experimental School, and the promotion of machine irrigation will aim to make the lives of farmers in this area better. The reputation of this area is getting higher and higher. This is the result of the efforts of the members of this society, but it is also the merit of the enthusiastic guidance of the Vocational Education Society. We must intensify our work in the future. Next, Jiang Wenyu gave a speech, hoping that members can exercise their powers and express more opinions on the society's affairs and participate in more work. Next, Huang Renzhi gave a speech, hoping that members can do good deeds, say good words, and become good people. Next, Wu Cuilun gave a speech praising the area's form and spiritual change, which is quite a model for the villages. Next, Yao Huiquan gave a speech on the benefits of using new agricultural tools. This area has been designated by the New Agricultural Tools Promotion Institute of the Vocational Education Society as a model promotion area, and it will surely gain great benefits in the future. Next, he reported on the business conditions of the cooperative rice mill and future progress plans. Next, the members expressed their opinions. Although their clothes were simple and their language was rough, they were able to abide by order and hit the nail on the head. Next, the committee members were re-elected, and Cai Wangzhi, Jiang Zhongjun, Zhang Yueren, Xu Deming, and Jiang Yunqiao were elected. Also, three alternate committee members, Cai Yunzhi, Jiang Jianwu, and Lu Wenhua, were elected.
